    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17311304765415282838">Available for the first time in the United States, this international bestseller reveals the secrets of nonverbal communication to give you confidence and control in any face-to-face encounter–from making a great first impression and acing a job interview to finding the right partner.<br/><br/>It is a scientific fact that people’s gestures give away their true intentions. Yet most o</span>
  <span id="freeText17311304765415282838" style="display:none">Available for the first time in the United States, this international bestseller reveals the secrets of nonverbal communication to give you confidence and control in any face-to-face encounter–from making a great first impression and acing a job interview to finding the right partner.<br /><br />It is a scientific fact that people’s gestures give away their true intentions. Yet most of us don’t know how to read body language–and don’t realize how our own physical movements speak to others. Now the world’s foremost experts on the subject share their techniques for reading body language signals to achieve success in every area of life.<br /><br />Drawing upon more than thirty years in the field, as well as cutting-edge research from evolutionary biology, psychology, and medical technologies that demonstrate what happens in the brain, the authors examine each component of body language and give you the basic vocabulary to read attitudes and emotions through behavior. <br /><br />Discover:<br />• How palms and handshakes are used to gain control<br />• The most common gestures of liars<br />• How the legs reveal what the mind wants to do<br />• The most common male and female courtship gestures and signals<br />• The secret signals of cigarettes, glasses, and makeup<br />• The magic of smiles–including smiling advice for women<br />• How to use nonverbal cues and signals to communicate more effectively and get the reactions you want<br /><br />Filled with fascinating insights, humorous observations, and simple strategies that you can apply to any situation, this intriguing book will enrich your communication with and understanding of others–as well as yourself.</span>

<a href="/questions/1834765-i-am-looking-for-a-book-that-will-help-me">I am looking for a book that will help me in interviews and in public speaking, and I am a visual learner that prefers pictures. I am also looking at &quot;Body Language for Dummies&quot;. Which one is best to learn from and why?</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I personally haven't read 'Body Language for Dummies' but I really would recommend this as a general read to learn a lot more about body language mann<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I personally haven't read 'Body Language for Dummies' but I really would recommend this as a general read to learn a lot more about body language mannerisms &amp; signals within a business sector &amp; for sure as a public speaker. Analyzing yourself &amp; audiences is displayed in such an easy way in this book. <br />You won't be disappointed. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_232298288" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232298288" />
    <a title="Jan-Maat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5617661-jan-maat"><img alt="Jan-Maat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407579968p2/5617661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232298288?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan-Maat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan-Maat" href="/user/show/5617661-jan-maat">Jan-Maat</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752858784" href="/book/show/161442.The_Definitive_Book_of_the_Body_Language">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=business-management-pm">business-management-pm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=british-isles">british-isles</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232298288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16869998579154069993">I am fairly sure this was recommended on a management course. Entertaining read, well illustrated. Not sure how accurate it is, I tried out some of the ideas such as sitting side by side or at an angle to somebody rather than opposite across a desk at them. I certainly felt better for doing so but then the book told me that I would!<br/><br/>The downside for me is that I started to become absurdly self-conscious. Was I standing in an optimum way, sending out the best messages? Were my feet pointing in the</span>
  <span id="freeText16869998579154069993" style="display:none">I am fairly sure this was recommended on a management course. Entertaining read, well illustrated. Not sure how accurate it is, I tried out some of the ideas such as sitting side by side or at an angle to somebody rather than opposite across a desk at them. I certainly felt better for doing so but then the book told me that I would!<br /><br />The downside for me is that I started to become absurdly self-conscious. Was I standing in an optimum way, sending out the best messages? Were my feet pointing in the right directions? If somebody's body language is negative should I try to counter it by offering them something to hold? Does any of this stuff really work or is it just silliness? Is the conscious embrace of silliness the most sensible approach to interaction with fellow humans?<br /><br />The serious downside is that there is a lot of assertions made in the book with very little evidence and what evidence there is tends to fall back on one study or one anecdotal example which leaves one wondering quite how generally applicable the guidance is, particularly outside of the UK. <br /><br />On the other hand having been the retreating party when talking with somebody whose notions of allowable personal space where much smaller than mine<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ from a distance and at the incorrect angle it must have looked as though we were dancing the quickstep  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I wish that this book was read more widely - I eventually ended up backed up against a wall trapped by a water cooler feeling distinctly unamused.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16869998579154069993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText17325467613391923578" style="display:none">Since childhood, I've always fantasized having the superpower of mind reading and ever since being exposed to a diverse set of materials on body language I can assert that I've actually cultivated some skills in this vain :D :P.<br /><br />This book by Allan Peace is the bible of the body language books and reference to many results you see when you google about this topic and covers a wide and thorough spectrum of topics.<br /><br />Here are some exciting skills and insights you will acquire after consuming the book and applying its knowledge:<br /><br />1. You will be able to tell if someone is genuinely agreed with you or simply is faking so.<br />2. It would be easier for you to see if someone is lying or hiding something.<br /><br />3. When to tell if your message being conveyed and that your subjects are open and receptive to your arguments. <br />4. How to use body language to power up your position, radiate a dominant outlook and literally be more effective.<br /><br />5. You can tell if someone is interested in you or others.<br />6. In the book, there are lots of mistakes pointed out to be avoided in business situations and especially has a lot of advice for women to obtain a more firm stance in their meetings.<br /><br />And much more interesting topics ...<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to anyone who seeks communication skills and wants to appear more competent in his/her social or business interactions as well as to those whom with high ambitions of having an upper hand in their day-to-day meetings with others.<br /><br />If you desire to consume more advanced topics in this subject, I'd also recommend:<br />• Emotions revealed<br />• Unmasking the face<br />• Telling lies<br />All by the psychology guru and deception expert: Paul Ekman</span>

  <span id="freeText11703251193447859243" style="display:none">Aside from there being misinformation scattered about, (Napoleon wasn't 5'4", George W Bush didn't get his first passport when he became president) the authors completely rely on logical fallacies to prove their points. <div id="review_2248982267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2248982267" />
    <a title="Raluca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2416724-raluca"><img alt="Raluca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555587540p2/2416724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2248982267?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raluca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raluca" href="/user/show/2416724-raluca">Raluca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781409168508" href="/book/show/35281662-the-definitive-book-of-body-language">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2416724-raluca?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2416724-raluca?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2416724-raluca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2416724-raluca?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2416724-raluca?shelf=nemucon-research">nemucon-research</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2248982267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6060141199721389161">3.5/5.<br/><br/>This book was very difficult to rate. On one hand, it's a pretty comprehensive guide of human gestures and postures, aided in their understanding by suggestive illustrations. On the other hand, I kept getting the feeling that the authors were trying really, really hard to sell me a commercial version of body language. Often, things were exaggeratedly emphasized in a clickbaity way and I would not have been surprised to see chapter titles such as: "You will not believe how your boss is domi</span>
  <span id="freeText6060141199721389161" style="display:none">3.5/5.<br /><br />This book was very difficult to rate. On one hand, it's a pretty comprehensive guide of human gestures and postures, aided in their understanding by suggestive illustrations. On the other hand, I kept getting the feeling that the authors were trying really, really hard to sell me a commercial version of body language. Often, things were exaggeratedly emphasized in a clickbaity way and I would not have been surprised to see chapter titles such as: "You will not believe how your boss is dominating you!" or "Seven ultra-secret signals she's into you!".<br /><br />Searching for information about the authors, I see that neither of them is a psychologist or scientist of any kind. They're just really, really good salespeople who've found their niche. That makes me a bit skeptical about the validity of the interpretations they offer.<br /><br />There are other clues that make me doubt the content. One is the studies cited at the end. The book often contained phrases such as "studies show" or "research says". However, if I wanted to read about the study mentioned in chapter X, point Y, and flipped the pages to the end of the book, surprise! Instead of showing the research in the order it is cited, it is shown alphabetically. That means that I have to wade through a few hundred cited sources to see which applies and I am pretty sure this was done on purpose. The other objection I have with the studies is that most of them are from the 70s. (The newest ones are from 2003.) That leads me to believe that a) a lot of this research has been debunked/updated/couldn't be replicated and that b) the authors purposefully selected only those sources that had a vague resemblance to the point they were trying to make and stretched the interpretation in a sensationalist manner.<br /><br />A few other things bothered me. One was the "old gramps who's trying to be hip" cringe humor. The second was the outdated examples and references - it really shows that the book hasn't been edited for a newer audience, but is still stuck somewhere in the 80s-90s (in mentality too). Then there were the problems I had encountered in the previous body language book I had read, although to a lesser extent here.<br /><br />First, the book had a really strong emphasis on <i>man vs man</i> or <i>man vs woman</i> relationships.<br />Second, there were very few references to <i>woman vs woman</i> relationships. (In fact, the authors presented a very petty/catty attitude between women as the only plausible one. What about female friends? Is the notion that alien?)<br />Third, all the interactions between men and women were interpreted in a sexual manner. (What about the young man arguing with the old woman in the bus over the position of the window? I bet the authors would say that the opening and closing of the window is a suggestive sexual allusion or whatever.) More so, women were seen as always submissive in their gestures in a man's presence. (I'm not going to go into that.)<br />Fourth, men were also presented as some sort of primitive grunting beasts ready to jump at each other's throats... OK, I am exaggerating, but the authors did seem to see them as very simplistic beings incapable of any kind of complex thoughts. (I find this particularly insulting.)<br /><br />Again, I think that most of the things mentioned in the paragraph above have a very high commercial value and while they might carry some form of truth (yes, there are differences between the two sexes), they have been exaggerated for the public, because this is what sells and this is what the public wants to hear/read.<br /><br />All in all, this was another book I used as research for the series I am writing. The best thing about it is that a) it's comprehensive (there are even chapters about mirroring another person's body language or height differences or seating positions) and b) it has useful illustrations. I recommend it to other (aspiring) writers, just be careful to take it with a grain of salt.<br /><br />(As a bonus, checking this book, I realize that my characters' body language has been pretty well-written, just too detailed and hard to follow at points.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6060141199721389161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115342219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115342219" />
    <a title="Ellen Maze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2898778-ellen-maze"><img alt="Ellen Maze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482938374p2/2898778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115342219?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen Maze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen Maze" href="/user/show/2898778-ellen-maze">Ellen Maze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People Watchers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2898778-ellen-maze?shelf=read-for-research-value">read-for-research-value</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115342219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12591369811759247470">As an author, I am naturally a student of observation, so this book had the potential to be of great service to me not only in my writing, but in character-building and expression. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the read. Unlike some other Body Language books, this one has a lot of photographs, and at the risk of sounding sophomoric, they really added to my understanding of the text. <br/><br/>The chapters/categories made a lot of sense, and the information moved along with little unnecessary repetition. I think everyone who </span>
  <span id="freeText12591369811759247470" style="display:none">As an author, I am naturally a student of observation, so this book had the potential to be of great service to me not only in my writing, but in character-building and expression. <br /><br />I enjoyed the read. Unlike some other Body Language books, this one has a lot of photographs, and at the risk of sounding sophomoric, they really added to my understanding of the text. <br /><br />The chapters/categories made a lot of sense, and the information moved along with little unnecessary repetition. I think everyone who reads this book will have their eyes opened, and begin to read body language everywhere they go. <br /><br />The only thing that bugged me was that the authors used evolution to explain much of the human's use of body language. I didn't find their theories believable, and evolution explanations really weren't necessary. I would expect some reference to the ape-man, Neanderthal, etc, but these authors referred to them with a fervor akin to proselytizing. This shortcoming is the only thing that held me back from leaving 5-stars. Skimming those sections was easy, and the book is well worth the read and the purchase price. <br /><br /><br /><br />Ellen C Maze <br />Author of Curiously Spiritual Vampire Tales<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12591369811759247470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_378235067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378235067" />
    <a title="Gabriela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8107877-gabriela"><img alt="Gabriela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357840506p2/8107877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378235067?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriela" href="/user/show/8107877-gabriela">Gabriela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378235067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7195146896288105525">Allan Pease and Barbara Pease apply their experience in medicine, biology and psychology to illustrate the workings of the brain and how this influences our body language. In the Definite Book Of Body Language, the authors show us how we can use our knowledge of the brain's functions to understand people's emotions and behaviors.<br/><br/>I have to say that neuropsychology and behavioral science have always fascinated me. There are many books out there about these topics. But I found this one particularly</span>
  <span id="freeText7195146896288105525" style="display:none">Allan Pease and Barbara Pease apply their experience in medicine, biology and psychology to illustrate the workings of the brain and how this influences our body language. In the Definite Book Of Body Language, the authors show us how we can use our knowledge of the brain's functions to understand people's emotions and behaviors.<br /><br />I have to say that neuropsychology and behavioral science have always fascinated me. There are many books out there about these topics. But I found this one particularly interesting as it covered real life examples which you could see yourself applying or identify body language behavior and what the other person in communicating. The authors have used real life examples and offer various exercises that you can undertake to practice reading people's emotions and behaviors.<br /><br />I would recommend this one to everyone really. Whether you are interviewer, a manager, a teacher, businessperson, someone looking for a job, or for a partner, this book can help you understand other people's behavior and perhaps overcome communicational barriers. It does serve as a great premier especially if you are not entirely familiar with the psychology of body language. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7195146896288105525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3244048556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3797486797758732781">I am not saying that if the authors claim "water is wet", you need to ask for a second opinion. <br/><br/>Ok I lied, you need to ask for a second opinion. <br/><br/>There are parts that are genuinely riddled with sweeping statements and superfluous information, but to be fair, there are also parts that actually are interesting and are based on psychological studies done on human behaviour and the resulting body language. The problem lies in separating the proverbial wheat from the chaff. Since some claims are quest</span>
  <span id="freeText3797486797758732781" style="display:none">I am not saying that if the authors claim "water is wet", you need to ask for a second opinion. <br /><br />Ok I lied, you need to ask for a second opinion. <br /><br />There are parts that are genuinely riddled with sweeping statements and superfluous information, but to be fair, there are also parts that actually are interesting and are based on psychological studies done on human behaviour and the resulting body language. The problem lies in separating the proverbial wheat from the chaff. Since some claims are questionable, all claims are questionable and it doesn't hurt to educate yourself on claims that seem too neatly packaged to be true. Winnowing and Google go hand in hand.<br /><br />So, in summary -<br />- Interesting read if you suspend scientific rigour and logical disbelief at certain points. <br />- Good book to skim through to get a better grasp on reading your audience or improving your body language but not one to be taken word for word and read through with firm conviction in all the claims made.<br />- Get a second hand copy for yourself and speed-read the book in a day or two.</span>

  <span id="freeText10387504044599200684" style="display:none">I rarely read every word of non-fiction books, but this is one of the rare exceptions. It's not even particularly fascinating. But it is interesting enough to hold my attention without skipping or skimming over anything. ALMOST four stars. It wasn't awesome enough to go out and purchase, but it would be great to have around all the time for reference when the fancy strikes. I doubt I'll remember this stuff on my own as well as I'd like to.<br /><br />I'm sure that for a few days at least, I'll be watching everyone around me to try to guess their secret thoughts like a mind-reader, ha ha! Next step, rule the world!<br /><br />Note: It appears from the descriptions in the book that I display some body language characterized by male dominance (for those who don't know me, I am a smallish female). Has anyone I know noticed this about me? I personally had never noticed. Does it unnerve you as the book says it would? I wonder if they are learned behaviors that I picked up because most of my friends have been male through my adolescence and young adulthood. I did not view myself as a dating option for them, but a social equal. Or am I simply more a more aggressive than average woman? Hmmm...makes me want to observe myself better.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6990791513650496841">I read (and still have) Allan Pease's original book <i>Body Language</i>. It is a fantastic insight into understanding the people around you.<br/><br/>I highly recommend this book to martial artists and students of self defense classes, because Allan discusses topics your instructors allude to, but quickly pass over, because they don't have the time to cover this subject in depth. <br/><br/>Realistically, anyone who has to deal with people should read this book.   <span id="freeText6990791513650496841" style="display:none">I read (and still have) Allan Pease's original book <i>Body Language</i>. It is a fantastic insight into understanding the people around you.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to martial artists and students of self defense classes, because Allan discusses topics your instructors allude to, but quickly pass over, because they don't have the time to cover this subject in depth. <br /><br />Realistically, anyone who has to deal with people should read this book. From a self defense point of view, it's easier to avoid trouble if you can read the people around you (but it does take practice).<br /><br />I purchased this revised edition a few years ago because it contained a lot of additional information. While it would be impossible to remember everything discussed by the author, it is definitely worth your while to absorb as much of the information as you are able.</span>

<div id="review_1987902716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987902716" />
    <a title="Lydia Howe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35587655-lydia-howe"><img alt="Lydia Howe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484415536p2/35587655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987902716?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia Howe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia Howe" href="/user/show/35587655-lydia-howe">Lydia Howe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35587655-lydia-howe?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35587655-lydia-howe?shelf=2017-two-star">2017-two-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35587655-lydia-howe?shelf=2017-nonfiction">2017-nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987902716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6823866652869745809">How in the world do I even rate this book? <br/><br/>So, let me start off by saying that I very much recommend people read books about body language. And then let me follow that up by saying this is not the book I would recommend reading. But, I do think this book was really helpful and it was eye-opening and for the most part it was really interesting. I'm glad I read it and I learned a lot from it and I will most likely be re-reading it and studying it from time to time to learn more. <br/><br/>Along with all tha</span>
  <span id="freeText6823866652869745809" style="display:none">How in the world do I even rate this book? <br /><br />So, let me start off by saying that I very much recommend people read books about body language. And then let me follow that up by saying this is not the book I would recommend reading. But, I do think this book was really helpful and it was eye-opening and for the most part it was really interesting. I'm glad I read it and I learned a lot from it and I will most likely be re-reading it and studying it from time to time to learn more. <br /><br />Along with all that good information, there was enough stuff in this book that was awkward, inappropriate, or wrong (nearly every page talked about evolution and I don't agree with that) that I wouldn't even be okay having the book sit somewhere where people could pick it up and read it. I bought white-out for me to fix a few of the issues (like illustrations that really aren't okay), so that was helpful. <br /><br />So, this book was helpful, and the information for the most part was stuff that I think was important to know (even when it was awko-taco) - I just wouldn't be okay handing the book to most people and recommending it. But body language as a whole? Yes, very important.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6823866652869745809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16357403190338366789">Undoubtedly insightful, and interestingly narrated, "The Definitive Book of Body Language" makes one conscious about the body language for others. Very useful book for salespeople.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1667864785712171350">A great book for getting an overview of how to improve your own & read others body language. Did that meeting go bad because you disagree so much or because you had unknowingly assumed a competing body/sitting arrangement?   <span id="freeText1667864785712171350" style="display:none">A great book for getting an overview of how to improve your own &amp; read others body language. Not only about making impressions of yourself on other, a lot more crucial takeaway here is about how you can create better turnouts for common goals. Did that meeting go bad because you disagree so much or because you had unknowingly assumed a competing body/sitting arrangement? Before telling my business partner about this example after having a few too intense meetings, I just switched up the seating arrangement &amp; worked like a charm - we found common ground on all our disagreements, and we’ll both appreciate body language more after this.</span>

<div id="review_55104761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55104761" />
    <a title="Carrie Wilson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2170861-carrie-wilson"><img alt="Carrie Wilson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322032410p2/2170861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55104761?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie Wilson" href="/user/show/2170861-carrie-wilson">Carrie Wilson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2170861-carrie-wilson?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55104761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3066501046790288128">This book is a well-researched summary of proxemics, gender and cultural differences in non-verbal communication, facial expressions and much more! A few tidbits you'll learn from this book: female brains are designed for multi-tasking (which is explains why we can watch TV, read a book, and chat online while drinking coffee); smiling is seen as a subordinate action and women tend to smile much more than men, something likely hard-wired into our brains; organs that are transplanted retain cellul</span>
  <span id="freeText3066501046790288128" style="display:none">This book is a well-researched summary of proxemics, gender and cultural differences in non-verbal communication, facial expressions and much more! A few tidbits you'll learn from this book: female brains are designed for multi-tasking (which is explains why we can watch TV, read a book, and chat online while drinking coffee); smiling is seen as a subordinate action and women tend to smile much more than men, something likely hard-wired into our brains; organs that are transplanted retain cellular memory so that recipients assume the mannerisms and gestures of their donor (!); in courtship, women are the initiators a whopping 90 percent of the time.<br />There is much more to this book--these examples are teasers. <br />The only downside to the book (and it is quite a small one) is that the authors list their references in the back in alphabetical order-- I prefer endnotes or footnotes or MLA style citation because I usually like to see the original sources for studies when I read non-fiction. Since this book is written for a general audience, I doubt many people are put off by their referencing style. <br />I also didn't care for the line drawings--again that is such a nit-picky criticism, but really! They could have done a better job with the illustrations. . . <br />I recommend this book to anyone human interested in fellow humans. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3066501046790288128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_605106027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605106027" />
    <a title="Cynthia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5218519-cynthia"><img alt="Cynthia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339529670p2/5218519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605106027?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cynthia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cynthia " href="/user/show/5218519-cynthia">Cynthia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605106027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10430487687374504631">I found this to be a very interesting and informative book. It's fascinating, and disconcerting, to read how many things we do unconsciously that are so denotative about our motives and thoughts. <br/><br/>Moreover, another intriguing concept is the fact that another person's actions, gestures or body language can engender a sense of benevolence, aversion or even hostility in us towards that individual, without us being able to comprehend why we feel that way.<br/><br/>The book is full of examples from real-life pe</span>
  <span id="freeText10430487687374504631" style="display:none">I found this to be a very interesting and informative book. It's fascinating, and disconcerting, to read how many things we do unconsciously that are so denotative about our motives and thoughts. <br /><br />Moreover, another intriguing concept is the fact that another person's actions, gestures or body language can engender a sense of benevolence, aversion or even hostility in us towards that individual, without us being able to comprehend why we feel that way.<br /><br />The book is full of examples from real-life personages, some of which are highly entertaining and amusing.<br /><br />It certainly teaches you a lot about hiding insecurities and looking more confident. And it definitely makes you much more aware about how you sit, shake hands or stare at a person. <br /><br />An enjoyable read recommended for all, but especially people who are interested in a career in business. They will find some very helpful hints and advice in this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10430487687374504631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fotIEmbGFuSBv7Z+mzLRa2lHBb+brrvh01gqv47o3fard8vi20OWqnv5eqt+wXTgeGkWDS43VAXqdILlPVBwUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

In Social Intelligence, Daniel Goleman explores an emerging new science with startling implications for our interpersonal world. Its most fundamental discovery: we are designed for sociability, constantly engaged in a “neural ballet” that connects us brain to brain with those around us.Our reactions to others, and theirs to us, have a far-reaching biological impact, sending out cascades of hormones that regulate everything from our hearts to our immune systems, making good relationships act like vitamins—and bad relationships like poisons. We can “catch” other people’s emotions the way we catch a cold, and the consequences of isolation or relentless social stress can be life-shortening. Goleman explains the surprising accuracy of first impressions, the basis of charisma and emotional power, the complexity of sexual attraction, and how we detect lies. He describes the “dark side” of social intelligence, from narcissism to Machiavellianism and psychopathy. He also reveals our astonishing capacity for “mindsight,” as well as the tragedy of those, like autistic children, whose mindsight is impaired.Is there a way to raise our children to be happy? What is the basis of a nourishing marriage? How can business leaders and teachers inspire the best in those they lead and teach? How can groups divided by prejudice and hatred come to live together in peace? The answers to these questions may not be as elusive as we once thought. And Goleman delivers his most heartening news with powerful conviction: we humans have a built-in bias toward empathy, cooperation, and altruism–provided we develop the social intelligence to nurture بكل اللي حواليك.. علشان كده الكتاب مقسم إلى خمسة أقسام..\n\nالقسم الأول (الفصول من 1 إلى 3) يخص تركيبتك أنت شخصيًّا.. اللي مهم تعرفها وتبقى واعي بيها قبل ما تعمل أي علاقة مع أي حد.. \n\nالقسم التاني (الفصول من 4 إلى 6) عن بعض الحاجات المهمة جدًّا في علاقتك بالآخرين.. هو إنت في العلاقة دي بتكون نفسك واللا بتكون حد تاني؟ طيب هو إنت شايف اللي قدامك زي ما هو واللا بتتعامل مع حد غيره في صورته؟ طيب اللي قدامك نفسه بيتعامل معاك كما أنت، واللا بيلبسك صورة حد غيرك؟ \n\nالقسم التالت (الفصول من 7 إلى 10) هانشوف فيه نتيجة اضطراب ولخبطة بعض علاقاتنا مع الآخرين.. خاصة القريبين مننا.. \n\nالقسم الرابع (الفصول من 11 إلى 19) عن التغيير.. عن الشفاء والالتئام النفسي.. عن قبول كل مشاعرك وأجزاءك من غير نقص أو تشويه أو اختزال.. عن قبول الحياة وقبول الموت.. عن امتلاء كل الفراغات النفسية اللي جواك.. والخروج من الصندوق الضيق المظلم المغلق عليك من سنين.. عن إنك تكون نفسك..\n\nوأخيرًا.. وبعد ما شوفت وحسيت واتحركت واتغيرت.. وبعد ما اتفكيت واتجمَّعت واتلملمت والتأمت.. هانستعرض في الفصل العشرين 30 علاقة خطرة مهم تاخد بالك منهم في رحلة حياتك.. علشان تبقى واعي بيهم، وتعرف تلقطهم وتشوفهم كويس، وتحمي نفسك منهم بكل شجاعة ومسئولية.. مهما كان التمن..\n\nالكتاب ده عنك..\nوعن اللي حواليك.. \nوعن اللي بينكم..       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/75844.Allan_Pease">About Allan Pease</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<span id="freeTextContainer3083676784100320935">Allan Pease is an Australian author and motivational speaker. Despite having no education in psychology, neuroscience, or psychiatry, he has managed to establish himself as an "expert on relationships".<br/><br/>Originally a musician, he became a successful life insurance salesman, he started a career as a speaker and trainer in sales and latterly in body language. This resulted in a popular sideline of aud</span>
  <span id="freeText3083676784100320935" style="display:none">Allan Pease is an Australian author and motivational speaker. Despite having no education in psychology, neuroscience, or psychiatry, he has managed to establish himself as an "expert on relationships".<br /><br />Originally a musician, he became a successful life insurance salesman, he started a career as a speaker and trainer in sales and latterly in body language. This resulted in a popular sideline of audio tapes, many of which feature his irreverent wit.<br /><br />His best-selling book Body Language brought him international recognition. It has been followed by several others. He is quite well known in Australia and during the 1980s he was an occasional TV analyst for political debates where he would analyze the body language and overall performance of the contestants.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allan_Pease">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allan_Pease</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3083676784100320935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
